Praised is our God who created us for His glory and who planted in us life eternal.
May He open our hearts to His Torah to do His will and serve Him
So we do not labor in vain nor shall our children suffer confusion.
The Daily Siddur
The following thoughts are presented by the Portnoy Family with the hope that it will nurture a con¬
cern for our most precious possession — the Jewish community.
Three countries contain the bulk of the Jewish communities of the world; the Soviet Union, the
State of Israel and the United States. Each one of these centers of Jewish population presents our
people with a different challenge and also indicates the heavy responsibility we bear as American Jews.
In Russia today one finds it difficult if not utterly impossible to be a Jew. Despite any discussion of
detente and the many calls for negotiation and communication with the Soviet government, the
undeniable fact is that we differ philosophically from the rulers of the Kremlin whose forced closing of
Jewish schools, and denial of expression of cultural freedom is part of a calculated policy of total
annihilation of Jewish identity. Whether these expressions take the form of kinship with the Jewish
people worldwide, or the celebration of a Bris when a Jewish child is born, or purchasing matzah for
Passover. Soviet government resentment is such that to be a conscious Jew in Russia today is
practically synonomous with being a martyr. Martyrs are not an easily come by commodity in the world
in which we live.
If it is extraordinarily difficult to live as a Jew in Russia, by contrast, one cannot help being a Jew in
Israel. No matter how weak the tie which binds the Jew to his people and his faith, the very atmosphere
of the Jewish faith serves to keep one Jewish. The Hebrew language, the many lectures on Bible and
Jewish literature within each community and broadcast over radio and television, the excitement in the
streets on the eve of the Sabbath, the closed places of business on the Sabbath and holidays, the
mezuzah on each door of Hebrew University . . . how can one help being a Jew amidst such
surroundings.
For us in America the question of remaining Jewish is different from that which is presented to the
other Jewries because for us, the decision is a completely voluntary one. Our country, thank God,
allows for the free expression of our faith and identity. Except for a few minor irritations we recognize
that we do not have to sacrifice our Judaism to be good Americans nor are we less American when we
practice our faith and identify with our people and their concerns. What we do have, however, is a social
environment which discourages the passionate expression of these Jewish feelings.
We are proud to be Jews, but we are not really sure why we feel that way. We want our children to
be Jewish, but we find it inconvenient to live a life in which these sentiments are translated into
convictions. We often want as a minority to blend with the major community and to eliminate these
characteristics, those expressions of faith and values which make us what we are.
American Jews are different from other Jews. Our Russian brothers CANT be Jewish, our Israeli
mishpachah CANT HELP being Jews, and we in America have the CHOICE of being Jews or rejecting
our heritage by sheer, cavalier neglect. To be offered a choice in any area of life means to be presented
with a heavy responsibility. We have it in our power to reject or to resoundingly affirm our way of life in
word and deed. Much of the fate of the Jewish people depends on our decision. What will it be?
EAST COAST FRUIT CO.
Walter Portnoy - Mrs. Louis Portnoy and Families

The merriment and all age participation of the holiday of Purim can be felt in the Synagogue while the
Megillah is being read. Always a capacity crowd, the holiday creates a joyous atmosphere the children
remember from year to year. The sound of the grogger and dangling jewelry, beards and mustaches,
three-cornered hats all add to the excitement. The following pictures were taken this past year.

ORT of Jacksonville
ORT, the Organization for Rehabilitation through Training, is an international organization which for a
century has brought freedom to world Jewry. ORT operates in 30 countries with 76,500 students learning
90 trades in 800 training units. They are people gaining an education and a future career in architectural
drawing, telecommunications, avionics, hotel management, machine design, computer technology, and
more, special programs are available for the physically handicapped, the aged, and language-training
programs for immigrants bound for English-speaking countries. Different courses for different people with
different needs and qualifications are offered.
Locally, we raise funds for the ORT program and participate in civic and Jewish community activities.
We strive to upgrade the image of vocational education in our community and to promote career education
in our school system.
Jacksonville Area Council helps support the ORT program and consists of five chapters that meet at
different times to serve the needs of all the women in the community. The Area Council is the body which
services the five ORT chapters. For membership information, contact Anita Warschoff, 737-7634.
The following are the officers of the Area Council and the five chapters and their meeting days:
Afternoon Chapter Meets 2nd Monday Afternoon Each Month
Beach Chapter Meets 1st Tuesday Evening Each Month
Beauclerc Chapter Meets 1st Friday Morning Each Month
Evening Chapter Meets 1st Tuesday Evening Each Month
Riverfront Chapter Meets 1st Tuesday Evening Each Month
WOMEN S AMERICAN ORT
AREA COUNCIL

Vice President.

Lewis Meisel
The River Garden Home is a vital, integral part of the Jacksonville Jewish Community. Through its residential care program,
River Garden serves community members who need a caring and socially supportive environment, including medical and
nursing care, in order to continue and extend meaningful life activity. The Short Term Program serves those who need
specialized care and rehabilitation in order to return to community living.
In its 35 years of service, River Garden has become a natural part of our community’s life cycle. Its presence assures
continuity of Jewish life style with continuing family and community ties to those for whom residential care is the best possible
life alternative.
The Home is situated on the banks of the St. Johns River, surrounded by gardens. River Garden serves the frail and ill aged.
It stresses the “wellness” of the individual. River Garden attempts to compensate for the individual’s deficits through its
medical, nursing and psychosocial services and attempts to motivate the individual to utilize his positive assets to the fullest
extent possible. Through individualized plans of care, the Home tries to strike a living balance between institutional
requirements and individual needs and styles. This positive accent on living, with a variety of social, cultural and recreational
programs helps create the special climate and tone of River Garden. This tone is also transmitted through the caring and
encouragement of a professional and support staff of 180 people, providing services 24 hours a day, seven days a week. The
families of residents and the whole Jewish Community complete this living cycle through active involvement and support of
River Garden.
For most of the Jewish Community the coming High Holidays motivates soul-seaching and reflection on the value of a
person and the meaning of life. At River Garden the entire caring community must struggle with these issues on a daily basis as
it strives to help meet the needs of those receiving care. We welcome all who want to join us in this deeply human involvement.
The first place to start is as a River Garden Volunteer.
On behalf of the residents and staff and the Board of Trustees of River Garden we wish the entire community a New Year of
Health, growth achievement and joy. L’SHONO TOVAH

CAMP RAMAH
Camp Ramah in New England, under the educational supervision of the Teachers’ Institute of
the Jewish Theological Seminary of America, is located just one and one half hours from Boston and
two and a half hours from New York City in the heart of resort and farming land. The camp is nestled
in the foothills of the Berkshire Mountains on the shore of a beautiful round pond, and surrounded by
thick forest. Boys and girls from age 9 (entering 4th grade) through 16(4 are eligible.
Your child learns the meaning of a way of life at Ramah as he experiences the riches of his heritage.
In classes and meaningful informal discussions he absorbs the abiding Jewish values. Hebrew becomes
a living language when it is an expression of the life of one’s community. Observance assumes a new
dimension when it has a natural setting of beauty and dignity and it is shared creatively with friends.
Personal ethics take on a new meaning when it evolves about the daily regimen of group living.
At Camp Ramah, your child chooses freely from a long list of available activities. He will learn new
skills and through them gain added security in his own world. The following is a list of typical activities
offered in a summer: acquatics, arts and crafts, dance, dramatics, music, nature, sports and synagogue
skills.
L/R: Melissa Roey, Stephanie Katz, Jonathan Gray,
Stephanie Gray, Sabrina Katz.
Not Pictured: Janet Jacobson, Judith & Simeon
Abramson, David Silverman, Dennis Mizrahi, Beth
Greenburg.
Abe Selber established in his will a perpetual trust for specific Jewish purposes. The proceeds from his trust fund are used
for Ramah Scholarships.
The family of the late Robert J. Gordon, of blessed memory, have generously established a scholarship in his name specifically
for Camp Ramah.
Donations to the Myra Thier Lazarus Fund, and the Sisterhood Ramah Scholarships all are used to help defray the costs of
attending Ramah.
U.S.V. on Wheels is not just another tour of North America.
It is a total experience of intensive Jewish living and educational
and social programming within the United Synagogue Youth.
Classes in Judaica directly related to the experiences of the
trip are held every day and are supplemented by special
interest seminars. The WHEELS itineraries visit the most
interesting, exciting, and diverse attractions and natural sights
on this continent. The plan has been prepared in careful con¬
sultation with experienced travel authorities including USYers
and advisors who have previously participated on WHEELS.
Any USY member between the ages of 14 and 18, who will
have completed the 9th grade by June 1981, may apply.
Registration is given to those whose organizational and
educational background indicate they will benefit most.
All USYers are encouraged to apply. Jeffrey Presser was lucky
enough to attend.
USY Israel Pilgrimage
For years, USY has been offering a summer in
Israel which incorporates living contemporary
Judaism, including Shabbat and Kashrut, with
the study of their heritage. In classes, on busses
on the hills of Judea, USY Pilgrims are exposed
to the history and contemporary realities of
Judaism and of Israel. The educational
process of USY Israel pilgrimage extends
Erica Jacobson far Beyond the formal classes; it is a living
experience. Climbing to the fortress of Masada, exploring the
grottoes of Rosh Hanikra, swimming the waters of Israel, singing
and dancing around the campfire, traveling from one end of
this wonderful land to the other, praying at the Kotel, have become
permanent highlights of our USY Israel Pilgrimage. Erica Jacobson
attended this year.
215

JEWISH CENTER SISTERHOOD
mrovnrara
U
3
fcLCUUACULU
As we begin a new admin¬
istration, we also adapt a
new Women’s League theme
to guide us during the next
two years.
Our theme is “Therefore
Choose Life!” These words
remind us that two ways are
open to us, one leading to
good and the other to evil.
In day to day contemporary Rcne c Gordon’ Sisterhood President
living, we are faced with many choices. Each of us has the free¬
dom to choose with wisdom, we must have knowledge. Learning
will help make each of us a better person, knowledge will
strengthen the family, and education will provide a deeper
awareness of the total Jewish community.
Through our Sisterhood Bat Mitzvah class, holiday
celebrations and up-to-date programs, we provide the guidance,
knowledge and awareness that our members desire in order to
maintain our Jewish ideals for ourselves and our children. Pri¬
marily our goal is to perpetuate traditional Judaism in the
home, synagogue and community.
We ask for your support and active participation in Sisterhood
now more than ever if we are to continue our glorious heritage.
L’Shana Tovah
Renee

HENRY KRAMER LIBRARY & RESOURCE CENTER
COMMITTEE MEMBERS
Chairman Minnie Schreiber
Co-Chairman TobiMeisel
Committee Roselyn Selber, Charlotte Glossman, May Goldie
Stillman, Clara Man, Diane Fages, Bess Rothstein, Anne
Shmunes, Hermine Newman, Florence Schreiber, Gene
Kornblum, Marilyn Mass, Florance Berman, Eva
Weinshelbaum.
The Henry Kramer Library has something for everyone-the Tofield
Room with its varied and great array of books with Jewish content-the
Solomon Schechter Day School Room with its many children’s books-the
attractive and comfortable Reading Room which encourages you to read
current Jewish periodicals and newspapers. It is indeed very accessible
and inviting and enlightening.
To celebrate Jewish book month, the Henry Kramer Library
Committee joined with the Adult Education Committee in presenting Dr.
Max I. Dimont, noted author and historian. Dr. Dimont’s book “Jews,
God and History” is one of the classics of our time.
The Henry Kramer Library Committee joined with the Sisterhood in
sponsoring an Oneg Shabbat featuring the literary talent of our own
committee members Tobi Meisel and Gene Kornblum.
In cooperation with the Solomon Schechter FTA under the
sponsorship of Marilyn Mass and Rhoda Goldstein the Solomon
Schechter Day School Library is being readied with the assistance of
Clara Mann, Florence Berman and Eva Weinshelbaum to meet the
increased reading needs of the Day School and Hebrew School students.
The Adult Library volunteers, May Goldie Stillman, Diane Fages, Anne
Shmunes and Bess Rothstein, under the guidance of Charlotte Glossman,
have devoted many hours to insure the smooth operation of the adult
collection.
New library related programs are being developed by Tobi Meisel,
Hermine Newman and Florence Schreiber.

SIMHAT TORAH CELEBRATION — SUNDAY, OCTOBER 14, 1979
CONGREGATION TO HONOR THREE LEADERS FOR OUTSTANDING SERVICE
HATAN TORAH
Judge Louis Safer
With a great deal of pride, the
Board of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center will honor Judge Louis
Safer as our Hatan Torah, the
groom of the Torah — the honor of
standing at the Torah as the last
chapter is read on Simha Torah. It
is an honor that Lou Safer truly
deserves.
Lou Safer presently serves as
Circúit Judge for the State-of Flori¬
da. As a practicing attorney for up¬
wards of 25 years Lou Safer al¬
ways had sufficient time (o share
his expertise, discernment and good
judgement for the welfare of the
Jewish Center. When the mortgage
was drawn for acquisition of our
present property, it was Lou who
served as our attorney carefully
watching out for the Center s best
interests. He also served the Jew¬
ish Center as the youngest Presi¬
dent in its history hut his dedica¬
tion and wisdom always set a fine
example of leadership for our con¬
gregation. When the Jewish Center
met on Third and Silver Strets and
two High Holiday services were
conducted at the same time our
honoree helped to conduct those
services. For many years Lou has
been serving as Chairman of the
Nominating Committee. Lou has
even filled in as a lay rabbi
when the Center was without pro¬
fessional rabbinic leadership.
Equal to the dedication that Lou
has shown at the Jewish Center
and community, he possesses per¬
sonal qualities of virtue and char¬
acter worthy of emulation. Always
a gentleman, thoughtful, considerate
and soft spoken, his easy going na¬
ture has made him a person worthy
of admiration.
Lou has set a fine example for his
family. His wife Marilyn, always
one of Lou’s greatest fans, shares
his commitments and dedication to
Jewish life.
His children Eliot, Cynthia Ba¬
ron, Deena and Shana, all look up
to their father and appreciate what
he has done for them and for his
community. Eliot Safer, now a
member of the Board of Directors
of the Jewish Center, is active in a
number of areas of congregational
concern.
We are pleased to honor Lou
Safer, a “man of conscience” whose
high ideals have truly made him a
leader of the community, and a
most worthy man to read the last
reading of the Torah. His quiet
personality and subtle humor have
earned him the love and respect of
his fellow congregants.
I
HATAN BERESHIT
Sheldon Gendzier
The Center Board is proud to
announce that the honor of Hatan
Bereshit — the honor of being at
the Torah at the time when the
congregation begins the reading of
Genesis, will be extended to Shel¬
don Gendzier. A tireless and com¬
mitted leader at the Jewish Center
and in the community at large,
Sheldon together with his wife
Horty and family have become so
closely identified with everything
good at the Jewish Center that this
honor is natural and appropriate.
Our Hatan Bereshit has served
most especially as immediate past
President of the Jewish Center. He
has however been intimately invol¬
ved with so many facets of our con¬
gregational life as their efforts on
our behalf are almost legendary.
An active member of the Educa¬
tion Committee for many years, an
important participant in the devel¬
opment of the Solomon Schechter
Day School, he still serves as Chair¬
man of the high school sub-com¬
mittee of the Education Committee.
Our Hatan Bereshit is not only
adept with gavel in hand, he is as
competent with a pencil and chalk
in hand sitting in front of a c’ass-
room, of bringing his own inimi¬
table style to a modern under¬
standing of Jewish history, Shel¬
don’s favorite passion. His willing¬
ness to volunteer is above and be¬
yond the call of duty and he has
brought the subject of Jewish his¬
tory to the attention of his stu¬
dents, young and old alike. Al¬
though it is true that a large family
always makes one sensitive to the
quality of Jewish education, Shel¬
don still continues to serve even
when many of his family members
are achieving their own new suc¬
cesses in business and at the uni¬
versity.
The concerns of our Hatan Bere¬
shit go beyond local concerns. Shel¬
don is a committed Conservative
Jew and, taking the example from
his father, our beloved Harry Gend¬
zier who was a vice-president of
the United Synagogue, Sheldon is
equally concerned with the affairs
of Conservative Judaism. A long
standing member of the Board of
what is now the Jewish Federation,
his interests are community wide.
Equally impressive is the under¬
standing of the Biblical injunction
of “honoring the hoary head of the
aged,” he is a past President of the
River Garden Hebrew Home for
(Continued on Page 41)
A WOMAN OF VALOR
Mrs. Jack Shorstein
In a fitting ceremony on the
morning of Simhat Torah the Jack-
sonvile Jewish Center’s “Woman
of Valor” award will be bestowed
upon Sylvia Shorstein. The religi¬
ous ceremony which will bring
Sylvia and her husband Jack to
our pulpit will give expression to
the Center’s recognition of Sylvia’s
many talents and activities on be¬
half of our congregation. For over
20 years Sylvia has been actively
involved in many areas of our
synagogue programs and activities.
Her first commitment began with
Sisterhood. Through the years she
has served as fund raising Vice-
President, Program Chairman and
Torah Fund Chairman. For many
years Sylvia has been an integral
part of the Center Board and ac¬
tive in its concerns. She has al¬
ways been generous with her time
and talents. Her warm and friend¬
ly disposition has been a great asset
to the Center where she served on
the synagogue’s Membership Com¬
mittee. She recently co-chaired the
Raffle Roast with Linda DuBow
and is presently actively involved
in the Interior Design Committee
where her excellent taste and aes¬
thetic sense are used to greatest
advantage. The many beautiful
Judaic items offered in our Sister¬
hood Gift Shop are examples of
Sylvia’s “sense of the beauty.”
By initiative and temperment
Sylvia’s concerns are broad and
general. She serves on the Gover¬
nor’s Commisison on the Status of
Women and is on the Board of
Directors of the Urban Library
Council. Her varied concerns and
interests also make her indispens¬
able to the life of Hadassah and
National Council of Jewish Wo¬
men.
As a wife and mother she is an
exemplar of a “Woman of Valor.”
She was of great help to her hus¬
band Jack over the many years of
his involvement in congregational
leadership and was most helpful
during the time that he served as
President of the Jewish Center.
Notwithstanding her many activi¬
ties, Sylvia created a fitting and
Jewishly warm home environment
in which she raised three fine sons,
Mark, Michael and Neal, who have
made their own impact inthe life of
our congregation, who are a source
of Nahas for her and who are in
turn very proud of their mother’s
accomplishments.
The synagogue’s “Woman of
Valor” award is our way of paying
tribute to a central figure in the
life of the Jewish Center.
39

TO OUR ADVERTISERS:
Our constant gratitude, not only for making the publication
possible, but also for the support they lend to our Youth
Activities. We urge our members to reciprocate with their
patronage.
• A reference and guide for the Jacksonville Jewish Center
membership and the Jewish community.
• Serves over 7,000 members and advertisers.
• All proceeds devoted to the Center’s program.
• The only Jewish publication in the community listing all
groups.
The Year Book is a summary of the various activities and
program of this Synagogue-Center depicted in pictures and
words. We are grateful to the many organizations of this
community who have cooperated in providing us with
material used.
We appreciate the efforts of our staff and other members of
the Center who have devoted time and effort on behalf of our
1980-81 Center Yearbook.
FLORENCE ROBIN
Secretary
DON MORRIS

ZIONIST ORGANIZATION OF
JACKSONVILLE DISTRICT
AMERICA
P O BOX 23780
JACKSONVILLE. FLORIDA
32217
President
Chairman of the Board ..
Vice Presidents
Membership
Public Relations
Programming
Projects
Education
Recording Secretary . . .
Corresponding Secretary
. .. Dr. Milton Mann
AlanTaffet
Robert Nied
. . Rabbi Gary Perras
Dr. Nelson Goldman
. . . Emanuel Ehrlich
Ann Shmunes
. . . . Laurie Benwick
Lillian Meizlik
BOARD MEMBERS: Jack Becker, Myron Dunay, Abe Fages, David Goodman,
Cantor A. Marton, Dr. Cheryl Rosenblatt, Dr. Elias Rosenblatt, Bess Rothstein,
Hyman Selber, Leonard Selber, Nathan Shmunes
L-R: Alan Taffet, Chairman of the Board;
Emanuel Ehrlich, Vice President; Dr.
Milton Mann, President; Joel Bressler;
Ann Shmunes, Vice President.
The Jacksonville District of the Zionist Organization of America is the only organization functioning
here at this time whose sole function is Zionist activity, especially the promotion and rebuilding of the State
of Israel. Our main fund raising function every year is for the Jewish National Fund at which time we plant a
grove of trees in Israel, usually in memory of a local person.
In addition, we hold meetings all year to coordinate activities involving programs, public relations,
membership, and response to media. The objective of Z.O. A. is to interpret and improve the Jewish and
Israeli position of our elected officials, to foster American support for Israel and to counter the Arab
propoganda campaign. Some of our more successful projects in recent years were our co-sponsoring with
Hadassah the screening of the smash Israeli musical “Kazablan”, a performance of the “World of Shalom
Aleichem” and most recently co-sponsored with the Minyanaires a weekend with Wolf Blitzer, United
States correspondent for the Jerusalem Post. Through the course of every year we bring in informational
speakers including Israelis.
We ask for participation from everyone since our national organization is one of the most effective
lobbying organizations with a constituency or membership, and the larger our membership the more
effective we can be.
241

Estelle Morse, Program Secretary
This past year was a landmark year in our Jewish
community. Through a constitutional change, the
Jacksonville Jewish Federation supplanted the
Jacksonville Jewish Community Council. The change
was made to provide a more representative format for
communal decision-making. In addition, the Federation
expanded its staff by adding a Dept, of Social Services
and hiring Susana Rothstein as its Program professional
The Federation efforts this year have significantly
changed the quality of Jewish life in our community.
The Federation will continue to provide services to
the community as in the past, and will embark in new
directions that will increase the quality of Jewish life in
Jacksonville.
The Federation will continue to conduct the Annual
Combined Jewish Appeal which raises monies for our
local agencies as well as the United Jewish Appeal and
national organizations. Our next Campaign will mark
our first ever one million dollar plus Campaign, a true
milestone in our community. The Federation has made
major increases in its commitment to both our local
Jewish Family & Children’s Services and the River
Garden Hebrew Home for the Aged. Our Russian
Resettlement program in Jacksonville has become a
model program throughout the southeast part of the
United States. The Jewish community, through the
Federation programs, has made a major effort toward
providing services in those areas where little has existed
in the past -areas such as Senior Citizen Programming,
Single Parent Family Programming, College Age
Programs, Jewish Singles in their 30’s and 40’s, etc.
The Federation provides a vehicle for service to our
community and it is the hope of the Officers and Board
that we unify our Jewish community for the betterment
of all individuals and organizations.

AFTER hearing a lecture by the late Francis Parker,
a great Chicago educator, a woman in the audience
asked him, “Flow early can I begin the education of
my child?”
“When will your child be born?” Parker questioned.
BORN?” she gasped. “Why he is already five years old!”
My goodness, woman,” he cried, “don’t stand here talking to me - hurry home! You
have already lost the best five years.”
This episode is an excellent commentary on the inspiring story of Hannah and Samuel
which we read on Rosh Hashanah. We are informed in the prophetic selection that Hannah
brought her child to the house of God in Shiloh when the boy was “but a child.” Hannah
intuitively understood what modern educational psychology has confirmed: the earlier
a child is exposed to spiritual values the deeper and more lasting these influences will be
in his life.
It is important that parents make every effort to surround their children from infancy
onward with the beauty of Jewish traditions. A child who has many meaningful Jewish
experiences in his earliest years will be given a secure foundation upon which to place the
ladder of education which reaches from earth to heaven.
An experienced outdoors-
man, Dov Kentof explains
various rope knots to youth
who constructed Tower
of David.

Marilyn Mass
Past President
MESSAGE FROM THE PAST P.T.A. PRESIDENT
The Marines are looking for a few good men. The P.T.A. is looking for a LOT of good parents. If everyone will
give a little more time than last year, attend a few more plays, then we can do better than ever as we continue our
old programs and develop some new ones. Giving of yourself is at least as important as giving your dollars. It
means so much to the children just to see or know of your participation.
Our P.T.A. is more important than P.T.A.’s in public schools. Our tuition dollars can purchase a great
teacher-student ratio, but they can’t furnish Federal support. In some cases, our P.T.A. provides not only
extras, but even necessities for a quality program. This past year we gave a great deal to the P.E. department so
that our students could have a better experience in that area. We have also purchased additional audio-visual
aids, needed equipment for classrooms, and even a sorely needed clock for the school office. We have
continued to serve hot lunches once a week and to provide traditional snacks for the Jewish holiday
observance. Our most recent project has been to get the library into optimal condition for our students’ use.
The manpower for this project has even included some people who do not have children or grandchildren in
our school. Hopefully, we can get some more help from our own parents.
Most of the money that we earned this year came from magazine sales. Our children were motivated (our
total sales topped Bolles’), and our supporters were generous. Some offices purchased hundreds of dollars’
worth of subscriptions. Lesser amounts of money came from our Book Fair, winter holiday day care program,
and birthday cupcake sales. We have benefited from our experience and can be even more successful in the
future with your continued and expanded support.
, Marilyn Mass, Outgoing P.T.A. President

Hodossoh
Hasassah, the largest Zionist organization in the world, as
well as the largest womens voluntary organization in the
United States, has a membership of 350,000 members who
dedicate themselves to help Israel, a developing democracy, to
help itself.
The Jacksonville Chapter has approximately 900 members
and consists of three active groups: TIKVA, which meets
during the day; HANNAH SENESCH, the evening business
and professional women’s group; and SHIR-LI, the young
women’s group which also meets in the evening.
The President’s Column
Shalom,
Leadership in Hadassah provides women with the
opportunity to share in the historic upbuilding of Israel
and thus enrich their own lives through service and
education.
Women for whom material comforts and possessions
are not life’s highest goals associate themselves with a
cause through work with an organization. No society in
history has had the variety and multiplicity of organ-
iztions which are to be found in the United States.
Everyone receives many appeals for membership in
organizations. Fortunately, vast numbers of women
have chosen Hadassah as the focus of their service.
Indeed, many have made it a central force in their lives.
Hadassah is more than an association of Jewish
women. It is a unique organization, a vital constituent of
the world Zionist Movement. It has made a major
contribution to American civilization and to the Jewish
people.
Leadership in Hadassah implies two things: the pri¬
vilege of standing at the helm of a great living movement
in Jewish history, and the obligation to absorb and
communicate to others the wealth of knowledge, ideas,
and ideals embodied in this movement.
Fondly,
Joan Waitz
Chapter President
TIKVA meets every 2nd Tuesday
Bess Rothstein 396-3898
SHIR-LI meets every 4th Monday evening
Tric ia Bloom 268-3989
HANNAH SENESCH meets every 2nd Wednesday evening
Gloria Weintraub 733-7370

ABRAHAM MARTON, CANTOR EMERITUS
Cantor Abraham Marton has served the Jacksonville Jewish Center
for 32 years before his retirement.
Although semi-retired, the Cantor is quite busy with visitations to the
hospitals, occasional services for Bar or Bat Mitzvahs, weddings, and
sad occasions in Jacksonville and surrounding communities. Cantor
Marton also conducts services on the High Holidays with a full chorus.
Plans are being made for a concert sometime in March.
A wish to everyone for a Happy New Year form Cantor Marton and
his wife, Pearl.
Cantor Abraham Marton and his wife, Pearl.
